============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG0)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P**c4
Candidate formulas: 75

GT (fixed function of **P** only; **no t-dependence**):
\[
0.953996983528\,(1-\tfrac{P}{96.9068829767})P + 0.953996983528\,P^{1/3}
= aP - bP^2 + aP^{1/3}
\]
where \(a=0.953996983528\) and \(b=\frac{0.953996983528}{96.9068829767}\neq 0\).
So GT is exactly a linear combination of three monomials: \(P^{1/3}, P, P^2\), with **no constant term** and **no t**.

Below, each candidate can match GT iff we can (i) eliminate any t-dependent/non-polynomial-in-P structure by setting coefficients to 0, and (ii) leave exactly the three powers \(P^{1/3},P,P^2\) with freely choosable coefficients.

---

### 1. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + P^{c3}c4e^{c5 t} + c6 t^{c7}\)
To remove t-dependence: need \(c1=0\) or \(c2=0\) (but \(e^{0}=1\) still leaves a \(P\) term OK), similarly \(c5=0\) or \(c4=0\), and \(c6=0\).
But there is **no separate \(P^{1/3}\) term unless** we set \(c3=1/3\) and also make the exponential factor constant (set \(c5=0\)). Then we can have \(P^2\) and \(P^{1/3}\), but the \(P\) term is \(Pc1e^{c2 t}\): to be t-free for all t, must set \(c2=0\) so it becomes \(Pc1\). Works.
So choose: \(c2=0,\ c5=0,\ c6=0,\ c3=1/3\). Then expression becomes \(c0P^2 + c1P + c4P^{1/3}\). Match GT by setting \(c0=-b,\ c1=a,\ c4=a\).  
**Matches.**

### 2. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P^{c2}c3e^{c4 t} + c5 t/(c6+t^2)\)
Need no t: set \(c3=0\) (or \(c4=0\) but still leaves \(P^{c2}\) term), and set \(c5=0\).
Then left with \(c0P^2 + c1P\). Missing \(P^{1/3}\).  
**No match.**

### 3. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + Pc3(Pc4)^{c5} + Pc6 + c7 t^{c8}\)
Remove t: set \(c2=0\) (so \(Pc1\)), and \(c7=0\).
Then terms are \(c0P^2 + (c1+c6)P + c3 c4^{c5} P^{1+c5}\).
To get \(P^{1/3}\) would require \(1+c5=1/3\Rightarrow c5=-2/3\), but then the term is \(P^{1/3}\) multiplied by \(P\)?? Actually \(P^{1+c5}=P^{1/3}\) yes, so it can supply \(P^{1/3}\). Great: then we have \(P^2, P, P^{1/3}\).
So set \(c5=-2/3\), choose \(c3 c4^{c5}=a\), choose \(c0=-b\), and \(c1+c6=a\).  
**Matches.**

### 4. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3 e^{c4\sin(Pc5+c6 t+c7)}\)
To remove t and non-algebraic dependence: must set \(c3=0\) (otherwise depends on t and on \(\sin(\cdot)\) in P). Then left \(c0P^{1/3}+c1P^2+c2P\).  
Set \(c0=a,\ c2=a,\ c1=-b\).  
**Matches.**

### 5. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{c2 t} + P^{c3}c4 + c5 t^{c6}\)
Remove t: set \(c2=0\) (so \(Pc1\)) and \(c5=0\).
Then \(c0P^2 + c1P + c4P^{c3}\). Set \(c3=1/3\), \(c4=a\), \(c1=a\), \(c0=-b\).  
**Matches.**

### 6. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2(Pc3)^{c4} + Pc5 + c6 t/(c7+t)\)
Remove t: set \(c6=0\).
Remaining powers: \(P^2\), \(P\), and \(P^{1+c4}\) (since \(P\cdot (Pc3)^{c4}=c3^{c4}P^{1+c4}\)).
To get \(P^{1/3}\): need \(1+c4=1/3\Rightarrow c4=-2/3\). Then we can match coefficients (combine \(Pc1+Pc5\) for linear term).  
**Matches.**

### 7. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3 e^{Pc4}\)
Must set \(c3=0\) to avoid \(e^{Pc4}\) term (not a polynomial/monomial). Then matches as in #4.  
**Matches.**

### 8. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3\log(c4 e^{Pc5}+1)\)
Log term cannot become a polynomial in P for all P unless \(c3=0\). Then matches.  
**Matches.**

### 9. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3\log(c4 e^{c5|P|}+1)\)
Same: must set \(c3=0\). Then matches.  
**Matches.**

### 10. \(Pc0 + Pc1(1-(Pc2)^{c3})^{c4} + c5(Pc6)^{c7} + c8\)
To match GT (no constant), need \(c8=0\). The middle term is generally non-monomial unless killed: set \(c1=0\) (or force it to a monomial for all P, which is not generally possible). Then we have \(Pc0 + c5 c6^{c7} P^{c7}\). Only two powers unless we also get \(P^2\) and \(P^{1/3}\) simultaneously—impossible with just one extra power term.  
**No match.**

### 11. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2(Pc3)^{c4} + Pc5 + Pc6\)
Powers: \(P^{1/3}\), \(P^2\), \(P^{1+c4}\), and \(P\) (from \(Pc5+Pc6\)).
To avoid extra power beyond GT, set \(c2=0\) (removes \(P^{1+c4}\)). Then match with \(c0=a,\ c1=-b,\ c5+c6=a\).  
**Matches.**

### 12. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + Pc3 + Pc4(Pc5)^{c6} + Pc7 + c8\)
Need no \(P^3\): set \(c0=0\). Need no constant: \(c8=0\). Need no extra power \(P^{1+c6}\): set \(c4=0\). Then left \(P^2(c1+c2)+P(c3+c7)\). Missing \(P^{1/3}\).  
**No match.**

### 13. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3\sin(c4\log(P^2c5+1)+c6)\)
Must set \(c3=0\) to remove sine/log. Then matches.  
**Matches.**

### 14. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3 e^{c4 t}\max(0,-P+c5)\)
To remove t and the kinked Max term: easiest set \(c3=0\). Then matches.  
**Matches.**

### 15. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + Pc3 + Pc4 + c5(Pc6)^{c7} + c8\)
Set \(c0=0\) (no \(P^3\)), \(c8=0\). Still have \(Pc4\) and \(Pc3\) (fine), plus \(P^{c7}\) term. But there is **no \(P^{1/3}\)** unless \(c7=1/3\). Then we would have \(P^{1/3}\) plus \(P\) plus \(P^2\). However we also have only \(P^2(c1+c2)\) and \(P(c3+c4)\): that’s fine. So set \(c7=1/3\) and choose coefficients accordingly.  
**Matches.**

### 16. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3\sin(c4 t+c5)\)
To remove t: set \(c3=0\). Then matches.  
**Matches.**

### 17. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + \frac{Pc3}{Pc4+c5} + \frac{c6}{Pc4+c5}\)
Rational terms in P must vanish for all P: set \(c3=0\) and \(c6=0\). Then matches.  
**Matches.**

### 18. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + Pc3\sin(c4 t+c5)\)
Need no t: set \(c3=0\). Then matches.  
**Matches.**

### 19. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2\sin(c3+c4 t) + Pc5 + Pc6\)
Need no t: set \(c2=0\). Then matches with \(c0=a,\ c1=-b,\ c5+c6=a\).  
**Matches.**

### 20. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + P^{c3}c4\)
To avoid extra power beyond GT, set \(c4=0\) (or make it duplicate an existing power). Already have \(P^{1/3},P,P^2\). Set \(c0=a,\ c1=-b,\ c2=a,\ c4=0\).  
**Matches.**

### 21. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^3c1 + P^2c2 + P^2c3 + P^2c4 + Pc5 + Pc6\)
Set \(c1=0\) to remove \(P^3\). Then have \(P^{1/3}\), \(P^2\), \(P\). Match by choosing sums: \(c0=a,\ c2+c3+c4=-b,\ c5+c6=a\).  
**Matches.**

### 22. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + Pc3 + P^{c4}c5\)
Need no extra power: set \(c5=0\) (or make \(c4\) equal to 1/3,1,2 and absorb, but simplest 0). Then match with \(c0=a,\ c1=-b,\ c2+c3=a\).  
**Matches.**

### 23. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + Pc3\log(Pc4+1)\)
Log term must vanish: set \(c3=0\). Then matches.  
**Matches.**

### 24. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3\log(Pc4+1)\)
Set \(c3=0\). Then matches.  
**Matches.**

### 25. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 e^{c3 t} + Pc4\)
To remove t: set \(c2=0\) (or \(c3=0\) makes it constant but still just another \(P^2\) term; either way OK). Then match with \(c0=a,\ c1=-b,\ c4=a\).  
**Matches.**

### 26. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^{1/3}c1 e^{c2 t} + P^2c3 + Pc4\)
Need no t: set \(c1=0\) (or \(c2=0\) makes it another \(P^{1/3}\) term; either is fine). Then match with \(c0=a,\ c3=-b,\ c4=a\).  
**Matches.**

### 27. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3 e^{c4 t}\)
Need no t and no constant term: set \(c3=0\). Then matches.  
**Matches.**

### 28. \(Pc0 + c1(Pc2)^{c3} + c4 + c5(Pc6)^{c7}\)
Has constant \(c4\) so set \(c4=0\). Remaining gives at most three monomials, but one is \(P\) and two arbitrary powers. To get exactly \(P^2\) and \(P^{1/3}\) simultaneously, set \(c3=2\) and \(c7=1/3\) (or vice versa). Then match coefficients by choosing \(c1c2^{c3}=-b\), \(c0=a\), \(c5c6^{c7}=a\).  
**Matches.**

### 29. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3 t^{c4}\)
Need no t and no constant: set \(c3=0\). Then matches.  
**Matches.**

### 30. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + Pc3(c4+t)^{c5}\)
To remove t: set \(c3=0\). Then matches.  
**Matches.**

### 31. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + Pc3\log(c4/(P+c5)+1)\)

### 32. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + \frac{Pc3}{P+c4}\)
Rational term must vanish: set \(c3=0\). Then matches.

### 33. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3\log(Pc4 e^{c5\sin(c6 t+c7)}+1)\)
t-dependent log: must set \(c3=0\). Then matches.  
**Matches.**

### 34. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + c3 e^{c4 t}\sin(Pc5+c6)\)
Non-algebraic and t-dependent unless \(c3=0\). Then matches.  
**Matches.**

### 35. \(Pc0 + Pc1(Pc2)^{c3} + c4 + c5(Pc6)^{c7}\)
Set \(c4=0\). Then terms are \(P\), \(P^{1+c3}\), \(P^{c7}\). Need \(P^2\) and \(P^{1/3}\): set \(1+c3=2\Rightarrow c3=1\) and \(c7=1/3\). Then match coefficients.  
**Matches.**

### 36. \(Pc0 + Pc1(Pc2)^{c3} + Pc4 + c5(Pc6)^{c7} + c8\)
Set \(c8=0\). Then have \(P\) (from \(Pc0+Pc4\)), \(P^{1+c3}\), \(P^{c7}\). Choose \(c3=1\) for \(P^2\), \(c7=1/3\) for \(P^{1/3}\). Match coefficients.  
**Matches.**

### 37. \(Pc0 + Pc1(Pc2)^{c3} + P^{c4}c5 + c6\)
Set \(c6=0\). Need powers \(P\), \(P^2\), \(P^{1/3}\): set \(1+c3=2\Rightarrow c3=1\), and \(c4=1/3\). Then match coefficients.  
**Matches.**

### 38. \(Pc0 + Pc1(Pc2)^{c3} + Pc4 + Pc5(Pc6)^{c7} + c8\)
Set \(c8=0\). Terms: \(P\) (from \(Pc0+Pc4\)), \(P^{1+c3}\), and \(P^{1+c7}\). Need \(P^2\) and \(P^{1/3}\): \(1+c3=2\Rightarrow c3=1\); \(1+c7=1/3\Rightarrow c7=-2/3\). Then match coefficients.  
**Matches.**

### 39. \(P^2c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + Pc3(Pc4)^{c5} + Pc6 + c7\)
Set constant \(c7=0\). The \(Pc3(Pc4)^{c5}\) term is \( \propto P^{1+c5}\). To get \(P^{1/3}\), set \(c5=-2/3\). Then we have \(P^2\) (from \(c0+c1\)), \(P\) (from \(c2+c6\)), and \(P^{1/3}\). Match coefficients.  
**Matches.**

### 40. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2(Pc3)^{c4} + c5\)
Set \(c5=0\). Need \(P^{1/3}\): require \(1+c4=1/3\Rightarrow c4=-2/3\). Then match \(P^2,P,P^{1/3}\).  
**Matches.**

### 41. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2(Pc3)^{c4} + Pc5 + c6\)
Set \(c6=0\). Set \(c4=-2/3\) to get \(P^{1/3}\). Linear term is \(P(c1+c5)\). Match.  
**Matches.**

### 42. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2|P|^{c3} + c4\)
Set \(c4=0\). To get \(P^{1/3}\) from \(|P|^{c3}\) would give \(|P|^{1/3}\), which is **not equal to** \(P^{1/3}\) for all real P (and GT uses \(P^{1/3}\) as written). Unless domain restricted to \(P\ge 0\) (not stated), cannot ensure equality for all P. Only safe is set \(c2=0\), but then missing \(P^{1/3}\).  
**No match (for all real P).**

### 43. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + P^2c3 + Pc4 + Pc5\)
Already exactly \(P^{1/3}\), \(P^2\), \(P\). Match with \(c0=a,\ c1+c2+c3=-b,\ c4+c5=a\).  
**Matches.**

Directly matches with \(c0=a,\ c1=-b,\ c2=a\).  
**Matches.**

### 47. \(P^2c0 + Pc1(Pc2)^{c3} + Pc4\)

### 75. \(Pc0 + Pc1(Pc2)^{c3} + Pc4 e^{Pc5} + c6\)
The \(Pc4 e^{Pc5}\) term is non-polynomial in P unless \(c4=0\) (or \(c5=0\) makes it just another \(P\) term). If \(c5=0\), it becomes \(Pc4\) (still only P plus \(P^{1+c3}\)). I need to determine which candidates are mathematically equivalent to the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.9540*(1 - P/96.907)*P + 0.9540*P^(1/3)`

Expanding: `0.9540*P - 0.009845*P² + 0.9540*P^(1/3)`

So GT = `c_a * P^(1/3) + c_b * P + c_c * P²` where:
- c_a = 0.9540 (coefficient of P^(1/3))
- c_b = 0.9540 (coefficient of P)
- c_c = -0.9540/96.907 ≈ -0.009845 (coefficient of P²)

This is a sum of three basis functions: **P^(1/3), P, P²** with no dependence on t.

Now I'll check each candidate to see if it can reduce to this form.

For candidates with `t`-dependent terms, those terms must be eliminable (coefficients set to 0). For candidates with extra basis functions (like sin, log, exp of P), those cannot be eliminated unless their coefficients can be zeroed.

Let me systematically go through:

Now for candidates WITHOUT P^(1/3) explicitly:

**Candidate 52:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + c2*(P*c3)^(1/3) + c4` = `P²*c0 + P*c1 + c2*c3^(1/3)*P^(1/3) + c4`. Set c4=0. ✓

**Candidate 53:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2 + c3*(P*c4)^(1/3) + c5` = `P²*c0 + P*(c1+c2) + c3*c4^(1/3)*P^(1/3) + c5`. Set c5=0. ✓

**Candidate 28:** `P*c0 + c1*(P*c2)^c3 + c4 + c5*(P*c6)^c7`. Set c3=2 → P²*c1*c2², set c7=1/3 → c5*c6^(1/3)*P^(1/3), c4=0. ✓

**Candidate 39:** `P²*(c0+c1) + P*c2 + P*c3*(P*c4)^c5 + P*c6 + c7`. Set c5=1→P²*c3*c4 + ..., but then we need P^(1/3). Alternatively set c3=0, c7=0 → P²*(c0+c1) + P*(c2+c6). Missing P^(1/3). [NO MATCH]

Wait, let me reconsider. Candidate 39 has no P^(1/3) term and no free exponent that could create one. The term `P*c3*(P*c4)^c5 = c3*c4^c5*P^(1+c5)`. Set c5=-2/3 → P^(1/3). Then: `P²*(c0+c1) + P*(c2+c6) + c3*c4^(-2/3)*P^(1/3) + c7`. Set c7=0. ✓
